>> GOOD MORNING EVERYBODY. NEE HOW IS WHAT WE'RE SAYING. NEE HOW AND GOOD 
MORNING. >> COUNCIL MEMBER TAMARA PALTIN. >> ALOHA KAKAHIAKA KAKOU, AND NEE HOW. 
>> COUNCIL MEMBER GABE JOHNSON. >> ALOHA, CHAIR, COUNCIL MEMBERS. \r\n\r\nCOMMUNITY 
MEMBERS. NEE HOW. THERE'S NO TESTIFIERS AT THE LANA'I DISTRICT OFFICE. MAHALO. >> 
COUNCIL MEMBER KEANI RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ. >> ALOHA KAKAHIAKA KAKOU, MAI MAUI NUI 
AKAMA. I'M SEEING A REPORT OF NO TESTIFIERS YET AT THE MOLOKA'I DISTRICT 
OFFICE.\r\n\r\nMAHALO, CHAIR. >> THANK YOU. >> COUNCIL MEMBER TOM COOK. >> ALOHA 
FRIDAY, CHAIR AND FELLOW COUNCIL MEMBERS. THERE'S NO TESTIFIERS AT KIHEI DISTRICT 
OFFICE AND LOOKING FORWARD TO TODAY'S MEETING. >> COUNCIL MEMBER NOHELANI UU-
HODGINS. >> >> GOOD MORNING, CHAIR, GOOD MORNING EVERYONE.\r\n\r\nNEE HOW. >> COUNCIL 
MEMBER SHANE SINENCI. >> ALOHA, NEE HOW EVERYONE AND NO TESTIFIERS IN HANA. >> 
RETURNING TO MEMBER PRO TEMPORE TASHA KAMA. >> GOOD MORNING. >> COUNCIL CHAIR 
ALICE LEE. >> NEE HOW EVERYONE AND ALOHA, WELCOME.\r\n\r\n>> CHAIR YOU HAVE ALL 
MEMBERS PRESENT, WHICH MEANS IN A YOU HAVE A QUORUM TO CONDUCT THE BUSINESS OF 
THE COUNCIL, FOR THE RECORD, I'M MOANA LUTEY THE COUNTY CLERK AND NEXT TO ME IS THE 
DEPUTY COUNTY CLERK, RICHELLE THOMSON AND PRESENT WITH US IS OUR LEGISLATIVE 
DIVISION STAFF, JOYCE MURASHIGE, LAUREN SALDANA AND DELL YOSHIDA, JOINING US FROM 
THE OFFICE OF COUNCIL SERVICES, IS DIRECTOR DAVID RAATZ, AND DEPUTY DIRECTOR RICHELLE  
KAWASAKI. FROM THE DEPARTMENT OF CORPORATION COUNSEL IS MIMI DES JARDINS, WHO IS 
THE FIRST DEPUTY AND VICTORIA TAKAYESU, THE CORPORATION COUNSEL. >> THIS MORNING, 
OPENING REMARKS WILL BE PRESENTED BY COUNCIL MEMBER TOM COOK. >> THANK YOU, CHAIR.  
THIS MORNING I WOULD LIKE TO ACKNOWLEDGE THE RESILIENCE, STRENGTH AND THE BEAUTY 
THAT HAS BEEN DEMONSTRATED THROUGHOUT MAUI COUNTY. OUR COMMUNITY TRULY STEPPED  
UP DURING THIS PERIOD OF CHALLENGE, GRIEF, AND TRAGEDY IN OUR COUNTY'S HISTORY. 
WHETHER IT BE BY LAND OR SEA, OUR COMMUNITY IMMEDIATELY ROSE TO GET NEEDED 
SUPPLIES, AND SHELTER TO OUR LOVED ONES, NEIGHBORS, FRIENDS AND EVEN 
STRANGERS.\r\n\r\nTHIS HAS BEEN AN EXTREMELY EMOTIONAL AND VERY CHALLENGING FOR ALL 
OF US. EACH IN OUR OWN WAY, I WANT TO THANK THE LAHAINA COMMUNITY FOR ATTENDING 
THE GREAT COMMITTEE MEETING LAS T WEEK. IT WAS HEARTBREAKING TO HEAR THE STORIES 
AND THE INDIVIDUAL EXPERIENCES, BUT ALSO INSPIRING TO SEE THOSE EXPRESSING THEIR 
THOUGHTS AND OPINIONS. IN LIGHT OF THE DISASTER WE AS A COMMUNITY NOW HAVE THE 
OPPORTUNITY TO MAKE THE CHANGES THAT MAY NOT HAVE BEEN PREVIOUSLY POSSIBLE. WE 
NEED TO STEP OUTSIDE OUR COMFORT ZONE, LET GO OF NO-CAN MENTALITY AND MOVE 
FORWARD WITH HOW CAN WE DO THIS ATTITUDE. THIS IS A TIME FOR US TO REVIEW, EVALUATE, 
AND REVISE OUR RULES AND PROCESSES. WE HAVE THE OPPORTUNITY TO MAKE A SIGNIFICANT 
CHANGES NOT ONLY FOR LAHAINA, BUT FOR ALL OF MAUI COUNTY.\r\n\r\nI'M OPTIMISTIC OF THE 
ESTABLISHMENT OF THE OFFICE OF RECOVERY, LED BY DEPUTY MANAGING DIRECTOR JOSIAH 
NISHITA AND THE CREATION OF LAHAINA TEAM. WE LOOK FORWARD TO MOVING FORWARD AS A 
COMMUNITY, REBUILDING LAHAINA -- WE'RE MAUI STRONG. IN CLOSING, I WANT TO RECOGNIZE 
OCTOBER IS BREAST CANCER AWARENESS MONTH. WE ALL HAVE WOMEN IN OUR LIVES AND 
BREAST CANCER IS ONE OF THE LEADING HEALTH CRISES AFFECTING ONE IN EIGHT WOMEN. THIS 
WEEK, OCTOBER 3-5 IS PINK WEEK ACROSS THE COUNTRY. SO IN HONOR OF THESE BRAVE 
INDIVIDUALS, I AM WEARING MY PINK TIE AS A SYMBOL OF MY SUPPORT. THANK YOU, CHAIR, FOR  
GIVING ME THIS OPPORTUNITY TO SPEAK.\r\n\r\n>> THANK YOU, MEMBER COOK. WELL-SAID. NOW 
MEMBERS, PLEASE JOIN ME IN RECITING THE PLEDGE OF ALLEGIANCE. I PLEDGE ALLEGIANCE TO 
THE FLAG OF THE UNITED STATES OF AMERICA, AND TO THE REPUBLIC FOR WHICH IT STANDS, 
ONE NATION UNDER GOD, INDIVISIBLE, WITH LIBERTY AND JUSTICE FOR ALL. MAY I NOW ASK 
THAT EVERYONE -- EXCUSE ME. BEFORE WE PROCEED, I LOVE THAT LINE. BEFORE WE PROCEED 
WITH TODAY'S AGENDA, MAY I PLEASE REQUEST THAT EVERYONE KEEP THEIR MICROPHONES 
MUTED UNLESS IT'S YOUR TIME TO SPEAK.\r\n\r\nORAL AND WRITTEN TESTIMONY WILL BE 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231006/231006.txt[10/26/2023 8:58:43 AM]
ACCEPTING AT THE BEGINNING OF THE MEETING AND PRIOR TO THE COUNCIL'S DELIBERATION OF 
EACH SECTION OF THE AGENDA. TESTIMONY MUST PERTAIN TO ITEMS ON THE MEETING AGENDA. 
WHEN TESTIFYING, PLEASE DIRECT YOUR REMARKS TO THE COUNCIL, AND NOT TO ANY 
INDIVIDUAL COUNCIL MEMBER, OR MEMBER OF THE PUBLIC. EACH TESTIFIER WILL BE ALLOWED 
TO SPEAK FOR UP TO THREE MINUTES ON EACH ITEM. DECORUM SHALL BE MAINTAINED AT ALL 
TIMES. ANY PERSON WHO BEHAVE ANYWAYS MANNER THAT DISRUPTS, DISTURBS OR IMPEDES 
THE ORDERLY CONDUCT OF ANY COUNCIL MEETING CAN AT THE DISCRETION OF THE PRESIDING 
OFFICER, OR A MAJORITY OF PRESENT COUNCIL MEMBERS, BE EJECTED OR BANNED FROM 
COUNCIL MEETINGS OR IF PARTICIPATING REMOTELY BE MUTED OR DROPPED FROM THE MEETING  
EXAMPLES INCLUDE, BUT NOT LIMITED TO HECKLING, SHOUTING, USE OF PROFANITY, 
THREATENING OUR SLANDEROUS REMARKS MADE TO ANY MEMBER OF THE COUNCIL, STAFF, OR 
GENERAL PUBLIC. AS A REMINDER THE CHAT SHOULD BE USED ONLY TO SIGN UP FOR TESTIMONY,  
AND NOT FOR PUBLIC COMMENTARY ON THE MEETING.\r\n\r\nIT WILL BE CONSIDERED A BREACH 
OF DECORUM FOR MEMBERS OF THE PUBLIC TO USE THE CHAT FOR ANYTHING OTHER THAN 
TESTIMONY SIGN-UP. MS. CLERK, PLEASE PROCEED. >> CHAIR AT THIS TIME, WE'LL BE OPENING 
TESTIMONY ON CEREMONIAL RESOLUTIONS UNDER SECTION D. IF THERE'S ANYONE WHO WOULD 
LIKE TO TESTIFY ON THE CEREMONIAL RESOLUTION AT THIS TIME, PLEASE LET US KNOW. WE 
CURRENTLY DO NOT HAVE ANYONE SIGNED UP. LOOKS LIKE MR. LAU MIGHT BE COMING DOWN 
TO TESTIFY ON THIS.\r\n\r\n>> CONDOLENCES TO THE FAMILY OF MIKE DAVIS, SR.. >> THANK YOU. 
>> CHAIR THERE'S NO ONE ELSE SIGNED UP TO TESTIFY. IF THERE'S ANYONE, PLEASE LET US 
KNOW. YOU CAN UNMUTE IF YOU ARE PARTICIPATING REMOTELY. AND THE COUNTDOWN IS 3, 2, 1 
MEMBERS, ANY OBJECTIONS TO CLOSING PUBLIC TESTIMONY AND ACCEPTING WRITTEN 
TESTIMONY. >> NO OBJECTIONS. >> SO ORDERED.\r\n\r\nMS. CLERK. >> THANK YOU, MADAM CHAIR,  
CALLING UP CEREMONIAL RESOLUTION 23-204, EXTENDING CONDOLENCES TO THE FAMILY OF THE  
LATE MICHAEL "MIKE" DAVIS, SR.. >> VICE-CHAIR SUGIMURA. >> MOVE TO ADOPT RESOLUTION 23-
204. >> SECOND. >> MOVED BY VICE-CHAIR SUGIMURA, SECONDED BY PRO TEM KAMA TO ADOPT 
RESOLUTION 23-204. VICE-CHAIR SUGIMURA, DISCUSSION. >> MAY I REQUEST THAT THE CLERK 
READ THE RESOLUTION IN ITS ENTIRETY. >> MS.\r\n\r\nCLERK. >> THANK YOU, MADAM CHAIR, AND 
VICE-CHAIR SUGIMURA.  RESOLUTION 23-204 EXTENDING CONDOLENCES TO THE FAMILY OF THE 
LATE MICHAEL MIKE A. DAVIS, SR.. WHEREAS, MICHAEL MIKE A. DAVIS, SR. A FORMER MAUI 
COUNTY COUNCIL MEMBER PASSED WAY JULY 1ST, 2023 AT THE AGE OF 79; AND WHEREAS, MIKE 
WAS A NATIVE MAUI RESIDENT, WHO SPENT MOST OF HIS LIFE AS A MEMBER OF THE LOCAL 
COMMUNITY AND WAS PASSIONATE ABOUT SERVING IT; AND WHEREAS, A DEDICATED PUBLIC 
SERVANT MIKE WAS A TEACHER AND STATE OFFICIAL BEFORE BEING ELECTED AS A COUNCIL 
MEMBER; AND WHEREAS, MIKE WAS BORN IN PA'IA, MAUI ON JANUARY 28, 1944 TO LUTHER DAVIS 
AND ELIZABETH WONG DAVIS; AND WHEREAS, MIKE HAD TWO BELOVED SISTERS, PENNY AND 
JUNE; AND WHEREAS, MIKE GRADUATED FROM ST. ANTHONY SCHOOL IN WAILUKU, WHERE HE 
EXCELLED IN A VARIETY OF ATHLETIC PURSUITS GARNERING LOCAL, STATEWIDE AND EVEN 
NATIONAL RECOGNITION AND HE LATER PLAYED SEMI-PRO BASKETBALL WITH THE MAUI 
WHALERS; AND WHEREAS, HE ATTENDED UNIVERSITY OF HAWAI'I AT MANOA AND EARNED A 
BACHELOR'S DEGREE IN EDUCATION, LATER GOING ON TO EARN A MASTER'S OF SCIENCE DEGREE 
IN PUBLIC EDUCATION FROM KENNEDY-WESTERN UNIVERSITY; AND WHEREAS, THROUGH HIS 
WORK IN THE VISITOR INDUSTRY, MIKE SHARED THE SPIRIT OF ALOHA AS THE PROPRIETOR OF 
DAVIS TRAVEL AND TOURS, AND AS SALES MANAGER FOR ALOHA AIRLINES; AND WHEREAS, MIKE 
ALSO SHARED HIS KNOWLEDGE OF MATHEMATICS AND ENGLISH LITERATURE AS A TEACHER AT 
MAUI HIGH SCHOOL AND; AND WHEREAS, IN HIS POLITICAL CAREER MIKE SERVED AS THE MAUI 
LIAISON FOR GOVERNOR JOHN WAIHE' E III BEFORE BEING ELECTED TO THE MAUI COUNTY 
COUNCIL FOR KAHULUI SEAT IN 1978; AND WHEREAS, DURING HIS COUNCIL TENURE MIKE SERVED 
AS CHAIR OF THE PUBLIC WORKS AND WATER COMMITTEE, VICE-CHAIR OF THE HUMAN SERVICES 
AND PARKS COMMITTEE AND MEMBER OF THE COMMITTEE OF THE WHOLE, LAND USE 
COMMITTEE, PLANNING COMMITTEE, BUDGET COMMITTEE AND GOVERNMENT RELATIONS AND 
FINANCE COMMITTEE; AND WHEREAS, HE DONATED HIS TIME TO MANY CHARITABLE 
ORGANIZATIONS SUCH AS BOY SCOUTS OF AMERICA, MAUI UNITED WAY, BIG BROTHERS/BIG 
SISTERS OF MAUI, MAUI CHAMBER OF COMMERCE AND MAUI JAYCEES; AND WHER EAS, MIKE 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231006/231006.txt[10/26/2023 8:58:43 AM]
LIVES ON THROUGH HIS THREE CHILDREN, MICHELE HEILE, MICHAEL DAVIS, JR., AND JONATHAN 
DAVIS, AND HIS TEN GRAND- CHILDREN LILIA, JAMES, AVA, SERENA, SUNNY, GABRIELLA, GINGER, 
SIMEON, HOPE AND SAM; AND WHEREAS, MIKE WILL ALWAYS BE FONDLY REMEMBERED BY HIS 
FAMILY, FRIENDS, COLLEAGUES, AND CONSTITUENTS. NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED BY THE 
COUNCIL OF THE COUNTY OF MAUI THAT IT EXTENDS ITS CONDOLENCES AND DEEPEST 
SYMPATHY TO THE FAMILY OF THE LATE MICHAEL MIKE A. DAVIS, SR. AND THAT CERTIFIED 
COPIES OF THIS RESOLUTION BE TRANSMITTED TO HIS CHILDREN, MICHELE HEILE, MICHAEL 
DAVIS, JR., AND JONATHAN DAVIS; AND THE HONORABLE RICHARD T. BISSEN, JR., MAYOR OF THE 
COUNTY OF MAUI; GOVERNOR JOSH GREEN, M.D.,, STATE OF HAWAI'I; AND THE COUNTY'S 
DELEGATION TO THE STATE LEGISLATURE; AND STATE'S DELEGATION TO THE UNITED STATES

EVERYONE.\r\n\r\n>> GOOD MORNING. >> MY NAME IS DESMOND CABILA, A SERVICE 
REPRESENTATIVE FOR THE HAWAI'I REGIONAL COUNCIL FOR CARPENTERS AND I'M TESTIFYING 
ON THE RESOLUTION 23-206 AND RESOLUTION 23-216 HAWAI'I REVISED STATUTES SECTION 104 
STATES ON THAT ANY PUBLIC WORKS PROJECT, MEANING ANY DEVELOPMENT, CONSTRUCTION, 
ROAD RENOVATION OR HOUSING PROJECT THAT IS RECEIVING STATE OR COUNTY FUNDING ARE 
SUBJECT TO PREVAILING WAGE RATES. THE INTENT OF THIS LAW WAS TO PROTECT THE 
STANDARDS OF LIVING FOR THE WORKING-CLASS PEOPLE INVOLVED IN THE CONSTRUCTION OF 
THESE PROJECTS ESPECIALLY FOR US IN HAWAI'I WHERE WE PAY THE HIGHEST COST OF LIVING 
EXPENSES IN THE NATION, THIS LAW PROTECTS US FROM DEVELOPERS AND CONTRACTORS FROM 
OUT-OF-STATE, WHO PAY THEIR WORKERS AS CHEAPLY AS POSSIBLE, AND THEN TAKING THOSE 
PROFITS, WHICH IS STATE OF HAWAI'I TAX DOLLARS BACK TO THE MAINLAND. THIS LAW H.R.S. 104 
LEVELS THE PLAYING-FIELD FOR ALL CONTRACTORS BIDDING ON PUBLIC WORKS PROJECTS. 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231006/231006.txt[10/26/2023 8:58:43 AM]
WHEN YOU COME TO HAWAI'I AND USE OUR TAX DOLLARS FOR YOUR PROJECTS OUR WORKERS 
DESERVE TO BE PAID THE AREA STANDARD WAGE, WHICH EQUATES TO WHAT IT COSTS TO LIVE IN  
STATE OF HAWAI'I. THIS IN TURN HELPS TO KEEP LOCAL FAMILIES FROM LEAVING THE STATE AND  
MOVING TO THE MAINLAND WHERE THE COST OF LIVING IS MUCH CHEAPER. THANK YOU FOR 
YOUR GUYS' TIME. >> THANK YOU.\r\n\r\nQUESTIONS, MEMBERS? IF NOT, THANK YOU VERY MUCH.

CONTRACTORS WORKING ON THE PROJECT THAT THEY PAYER LABORER AND MECHANIC NO LESS

RESOLUTION 23-214 THIS RESOLUTION, THE SAME REQUEST. THESE ARE EXPERIMENTAL AND 
DEMONSTRATION HOUSING PROJECTS AND BY LAW, THEY REQUIRE COMPLIANCE WITH CHAPTER 
104 AS WELL. CHAPTER 104 IS IMPORTANT, BECAUSE THE PAYMENT OF PREVAILING WAGES WILL 
HELP WITH MAUI'S RECOVERY, BY NOT ONLY INCENTIVIZING MAUI RESIDENTS TO JOIN THE 
LABOR FORCE TO BUILD MORE HOMES ON MAUI, BUT ALSO IT KEEPS RESIDENTS OFF OF WELFARE 
AND OTHER GOVERNMENT ASSISTANCE PROGRAMS, HELPS TO STIMULATE THE ECONOMY AND 
PROVIDE ECONOMIC STABILITY FOR WORKERS, AND THEIR FAMILIES. IF WE DON'T INCENTIVIZE 
MAUI RESIDENTS TO JOIN THE WORKFORCE, THAN WHAT IS GOING TO HAPPEN AND WE SEE IT 
HAPPEN, IS THAT OUR LABOR FORCE WILL BE IMPORTED FROM OTHER PLACES. SO LOCAL PEOPLE 
WILL BE WITHOUT JOBS, AND A LOT OF TIMES WHEN IMPORTED LABOR COMES IN, THERE'S LOW 
WAGES, AND THERE'S A LOT OF CUTTING CORNERS, NOT PAYING WORKERS COMP, TAXES, G.E.T.

THANK YOU, MADAM CHAIR. RESOLUTION 23-215, URGING GOVERNOR GREEN TO POSTPONE THE 
RE-OPENING OF TOURISTS TO WEST MAUI ON OCTOBER 8TH WHEREAS, ON AUGUST 8TH LAHAINA 
FACED AN UNPRECEDENTED AND DEVASTATING WILDFIRE THAT LEFT A TRIAL OF DESTRUCTION 
IN ITS WAKE, AFFECTING THE LIVES AND HOMES OF THOUSANDS OF RESIDENCES AND WHEREAS, 
THIS CATASTROPHIC EVENT RESULTED IN THE DISPLACEMENT OF A SIGNIFICANT PORTION OF OUR  
COMMUNITY WITH MANY RESIDENTS LOSING THEIR HOMES AND POSSESSIONS, LEAVING THEM IN 
A STATE OF PROFOUND UNCERTAINTY AND DISTRESS; AND WHEREAS, THE RECOVERY PROCESS 
FOLLOWING SUCH A TRAUMATIC EVENT REQUIRES TIME, COMPASSION, AND A SUPPORTIVE 
ENVIRONMENT, THAT ALLOWS RESIDENTS TO HEAL, REBUILD, AND REGAIN A SENSE OF 
NORMALCY; AND WHEREAS, THE RE-OPENING OF WEST MAUI FOR TOURISM ON OCTOBER 8TH 2023 
AS CURRENTLY ANNOUNCED BY GOVERNOR GREEN POSES A SIGNIFICANT CHALLENGE TO THE 
EMOTIONAL WELL-BEING AND READINESS OF OUR COMMUNITY MEMBERS, PARTICULARLY THOSE 
DIRECTLY AFFECTED BY THE WILDFIRES; AND WHEREAS, THE MAWK MAK COUNTY GOVERNMENT 
RELATIONS, ETHICS, AND TRANSPARENCY COMMITTEE RECEIVED OVER SO HOURS' OF TESTIMONY 
ON SEPTEMBER 27TH IN KA'ANAPALI DIRECTLY HEARING FROM LAHAINA RESIDENTS AND 
COMMUNITY MEMBERS AT-LARGE; AND WHEREAS, THE VOICES OF THE RESIDENTS WHO HAVE 
ENDURED IMMEASURABLE HARDSHIP AND LOSS, ECHO A PROFOUND NEED FOR EMPATHY, 
UNDERSTANDING AND PERIOD THAT ALLOWS THEM TO HEAL, REGAIN STRENGTH, AND 
ULTIMATELY SHARE ALOHA FROM A PLACE OF STRENGTH AND RESILIENCE; AND WHEREAS, THE 
ESSENCE OF THE HAWAII'S REPUTATION LIVES IN THE 'OLELO NO'EAU ALOHA AKU, ALOHA MAI 
AND ASKING INDIVIDUALS WHO HAVE NOT HAD THE OPPORTUNITY TO GRIEVE, RETURN TO THEIR 
PROPERTIES OR ENSURE STABLE CHILD-CARE AND SCHOOLING FOR THEIR CHILDR EN TO EXTEND 
ALOHA UNDER SUCH CIRCUMSTANCES COULD INADVERTENTLY JEOPARDIZE THE WELCOMING 
REPUTATION, WHICH OUR TOURISM INDUSTRY HEAVILY RELIES ,AND WHEREAS, IN A STAR 
ADVERTISER ARTICLE PUBLISHED ON PLEASANT HOLIDAYS PRESIDENT AND CEO JACK RICHARDS 
STATED, MOST PEOPLE ON VACATION WANT TO BE OUT CELEBRATING OPENING AND WITHOUT 
CRITICISM. IT'S GOING TO BE IMPORTANT TO MAKE VISITORS FEEL WELCOME AND TO RE-OPEN 
ENOUGH WEST MAUI BUSINESSES ESPECIALLY LUAUS, SO THAT VISITORS HAVE ENOUGH TO DO;" 
AND WHEREAS, RESIDENTS DESCRIBED MULTIPLE INCIDENTS UNDERSCORING THE TENSIONS THAT  
CAN ARISE BETWEEN TOURISTS AND LOCAL RESIDENTS WHEN OUTSIDERS UNAWARES OF THE 
SYSTEMATIC STRESSORS AND CHALLENGES FACED BY MARGINALIZED POPULATIONS ENCOUNTER 
AN ENVIRONMENT FRAUGHT WITH EMOTIONAL STRAIN; AND WHEREAS, THE TENSION BETWEEN 
TOURISTS AND LOCALS HAS ALREADY BEGUN TO SURFACE RAISING CONCERNS THAT THESE 
INCIDENTS MAY ESCALATE WITHOUT CAREFUL CONSIDERATION, FURTHER STRAINING THE 
DELICATE BALANCE BETWEEN TOURISM AND LOCAL COMMUNITY; AND WHEREAS, THE 
PRECEDENT SET IN UNITED STATES V. ALO-KAONOHI REMINDS US THAT WE MUST BE

RESOLUTION IN THE ENGLISH TRANSLATION, RESOLUTION 23-216,URGING THE GOVERNOR TO 
UPHOLD THE CONSTITUTION OF THE S TATE OF HAWAI'I AND THE STATE WATER CODE BY 
IMMEDIATELY REINSTATING MARVIN KALEO MANUEL AS FIRST DEPUTY FOR THE COMMISSION ON  
WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT. WHEREAS, THE STATE HAS AN OBLIGATION TO PROTECT, 
CONTROL AND REGULATE THE USE OF HAWAII'S WATER RESOURCES FOR THE BENEFITS OF ITS 
PEOPLE, AS MANDATED BY THE HAWAI'I STATE CONSTITUTION; AND WHEREAS, UNDER ARTICLE 
XI, SECTION OF THE STATE CONSTITUTION, THE LEGISLATURE SHALL PROVIDE FOR WATER 
RESOURCES AGENCY, WHICH, AS PROVIDED BY LAW, SHALL SET OVERALL WATER 
CONSERVATION, QUALITY AND USE POLICIES, DEFINE BENEFICIAL AND REASONABLE USES, 
PROTECT GROUND AND SURFACE WATER RESOURCES, WATERSHEDS AND NATURAL STREAM 
ENVIRONMENTS, ESTABLISH CHRIST RAW FOR WATER USE PRIORITIES WHILE ASSURING 
APPURTENANT RIGHTS AND RIGHT AS EXISTING CORRELATIVE AND RIPARIAN USE AS YOU 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231006/231006.txt[10/26/2023 8:58:43 AM]
ESTABLISH PROCEDURES FOR REGULATING ALL USES OF HAWAI'I'S WATER RESOURCE AREA; AND 
WHEREAS, IN 1987 THE HAWAI'I STATE LEGISLATURE ENACTED THE STATE WATER CODE CHAPTER 
174C, HAWAI'I REVISED STATUTES WHICH STATES "ADEQUATE PROVISION SHALL BE MADE FOR 
THE PROTECTION OF RATIONAL AND CULTURAL HAWAIIAN RIGHTS AND FOP THE PROTECTION 
AND PROCREATION OF FISH AND WILDLIFE THE MAINTENANCE OF PROPERLY ECOLOGICAL 
BALANCE AND SCENIC BEAUTY AND THE PRESERVATION AND ENHANCEMENTS OF WATERS FOR 
THE STATE OF MUNICIPAL USES OF PUBLIC RECREATION, PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY, AGRICULTURE 
AND NAVIGATION; AND WHEREAS, CHAPTER 174C HAWAI'I REVISED STATUTES ESTABLISHED THE 
COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT COMPOSES OF VOLUNTEER EXPERTS IN WATER  
MANAGEMENT, TO OVERSEE THE IMPLEMENTATION OF THE WATER CODE; AND WHEREAS, IN 
HAWAI'I WAI IS ESSENTIAL TO ALL LIFE AND PUBLIC TRUST MAKING THE STATE RESPONSIBLE FOR  
PROTECTING IT TO THE BENEFIT OF ALL ITS CITIZENS; AND WHEREAS, THE MAUI ISLAND WATER 
USE AND DEVELOPMENT PLAN WAS DRAFTED BY MAUI DEPARTMENT OF WATER SUPPLY 
RECOMMENDED BY THE BOARD OF WATER SUPPLY APPROVED BY THE COUNCIL, ADOPTED BY 
THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT TO PLAN FOR THE PROTECTION, 
MANAGEMENT AND USE OF WATER RESOU RCES ON MAUI BY THE WATER USERS OVER A 20-YEAR 
PERIOD; AND WHEREAS, THE MAUI ISLAND WATER USE AND DEVELOPMENT PLAN ESTABLISHES 
THE FOLLOWING FIVE POLICIES TO ENHANCE STREAM VITALITY WHILE BALANCING COMMUNITY 
NEEDS PROTECT AND ENHANCE NATURAL STREAM BEDS AND DISCOURAGE STREAM ALTERATION, 
WORK WITH THE APPROPRIATE AGENCIES TO ESTABLISH MINIMUM STREAM FLOW LEVELS AND 
ENSURE ADEQUATE STREAM FLOW TO SUSTAIN RIPARIAN ECOSYSTEMS TRADITIONAL KALO 
CULTIVATION AND SELF-SUSTAINING AHUPUA'A. RESPECT AND PARTICIPATE IN THE RESOLUTION 
OF NATIVE HAWAIIAN RESIDUAL LAND AND WATER RIGHTS ISSUES INCLUDING KULEANA LANDS, 
CEDED LANDS AND HISTORIC AGRICULTURAL AND GATHER RIGHTS ENSURE THAT STREAM FLOWS  
IMPLEMENT LAWS AND POLICIES FOUND IN THE STATE CONSTITUTION AND WATER CODE AND 
WORK WITH THE APPROPRIATE AGENCIES AND STAKEHOLDERS TO ESTABLISH MINIMUM STREAM 
FLOW LEVELS PROMOTE ACTIONS TO SUPPORT RIPARIAN HABITAT AND USE OF AVAILABLE LO'I 
AND MAINTAIN ADEQUATE FLOWS FOR THE PRODUCTION OF HEALTHY KALO CROPS; AND 
WHEREAS, THE COUNTYWIDE POLICY PLAN MAKES IT AN OBJECT TO IMPROVE THE MAJORITY OF 
WATER SYSTEMS SO THAT SURFACE WATER AND GROUNDWATER RESOURCES ARE NOT 
DEGRADED BY OVERALL USE OR POLLUTION; AND WHEREAS, THE WEST MAUI COMMUNITY PLAN 
ENCOURAGES EXPANDING LO'I RESTORATION, DECREASING SURFACE WATER DIVERSIONS AND 
ENSURING WATER FOR FIRE PROTECTION OF HOMES ON KULEANA LANDS; AND WHEREAS, LO'I 
REQUIRE CONTINUOUSLY FLOWING WATER TO SUSTAIN THE CROPS GROWN WITHIN AND AS A 
REGENERATIVE SYSTEM MAXIMIZING AQUIFER RECHARGE AND CREATES AHUPUA'A ECOSYSTEM 
THAT CULTIVATES AN ABUNDANCE NATIVE PLANT AND ANIMALS; AND WHEREAS, THE SYSTEMS 
THAT MADE IT A THRIVING AHUPUA'A, WHERE DESTROYED IN THE LATE 1800S AND EARLY 1900S 
WHEN PLANTATION OWNERS DIVERTED TENS OF MILLIONS OF GALLONS OF WATER A DAY FROM 
STEAMS TO GROW THEIR CROPS DISPLACING NATIVE HAWAIIANS AND CHANGING MAUI'S SOCIO-
ECONOMIC AND CULTURAL LANDSCAPE; AND WHEREAS, IN 1988, AND 1989 THE COMMISSION ON 
WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT DEFINED ADMINISTRATIVE RULES GOVERNING INTERIM 
INSTREAM FLOW STANDARD KNOWN AS IIFS, BUT THESE STANDARDS WERE FOR STATUS QUO 
CONDITIONS AND WHICH THE MOST CASES WERE DIVERSIONS OF ALL BASE STREAM FLOWS; AND 
WHEREAS, IN 2000 THE HAWAI'I SUPREME COURT OVERRULED THE COMMISSION ON ITS 
JUDGEMENT ON THE WAIAOLE DITCH CONTESTED CASE AND THE COURT HELD THAT THE 
CURRENT IIFS WERE NOT ADEQUATE TO PROTECT STREAMS OR COMPLY WITH AND REQUIRED 
COMMISSION TO TAKE IMMEDIATE STEPS TO ASSESS THE STREAM FLOW CHARACTERISTICS AND 
DEVELOP QUANTITATIVE IIFS STATEWIDE; AND WHEREAS, MARVIN KALEO MANUEL SERVED AS 
FIRST DEPUTY FOR THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT FROM JANUARY 28, 
2019 UNTIL GOVERNOR GREEN, AND DAWN CHANG, CHAIRPERSON OF THE BOARD OF LAND AND 
NATURAL RESOURCES REDEPLOYED HIM ON AUGUST 16, 2023; AND WHEREAS, DEPUTY MANUEL'S 
TIME AS DEPUTY OF THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT IS SEEN BY THE 
MEMBERS OF THE COMMUNITY AS ONE OF THE MOST PRODUCTIVE TIMES FOR THE COMMISSION; 
AND WHEREAS, IN APRIL 2022, WITH DEPUTY MANUEL'S ASSISTANCE, THE COMMISSION APPROVED 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231006/231006.txt[10/26/2023 8:58:43 AM]
THE ESTABLISH OF THE FIVE IIFS FOR THE ISLAND OF MOLOKA'I, RETURNING WATER BACK TO 
EAST KAWELA, EAST KAWELA TRIBUTARIES, WEST KAWELA, LUALOHE AND WAIKOLU STREAM, 
WHICH HAD BEEN ALMOST FULLY DIVERTED AND OFTEN DRY FOR MORE THAN A CENTURY; AND 
WHEREAS, IN APRIL 2022, THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT ALSO DIRECTED 
LAUNIUPOKO IRRIGATION COMPANY, INC. AS A SUBSIDIARY OF THE WEST MAUI LAND COMPANY, 
INC. TO RETURN WATER TO THE KAUA'ULA VALLEY AFTER THEY FAILED TO MEET IIFS AND TURN 
OFF WATER WITHOUT NOTICE OR EXPLANATION TO RESIDENTS AND WHEREAS, AFTER DECADES 
OF COMMUNITY ADVOCACY AND CLEAR ENVIRONMENTAL DEGRADATION OF THE AREA, ABSENT 
NECESSARY PROTECTIONS THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT PUT FORWARD 
ITS OWN PROPOSAL TO DESIGNATE THE LAHAINA AQUIFER SECTOR AREA AS SURFACE WATER 
AND GROUNDWATER MANAGEMENT AREA BASED ON DATA COLLECTED AND ANALYZED BY 
DEPUTY MANUEL AND STAFF AND UNANIMOUSLY SUPPORTED IN JUNE OF 2022, WHEREAS, DEPUTY  
MANUEL RECOGNIZED THE URGENCY OF ACTING TO DESIGNATE LAHAINA, AS IN DECEMBER 2021 
THE HONOKOWAI PORTION OF THE AQUIFER HAD PRIVATE ENTITIES WITHDRAWING 6.5 MILLION 
GALLONS PER DAY IN EXCESS OF SUSTAINABILITY YIELD BY 6 MILLION GALLONS PER DAY AND 
MAXIMUM AMOUNT THAT CAN BE WITHDRAWN WITHOUT RISKING PERMANENT HARM; AND 
WHEREAS, THE AUTHORIZED PLANNED USE OF GROUNDWATER IN THE HONOKOWAI AQUIFER 
EXCEEDED THE SUSTAINABILITY YIELD OF 51% AND THE LAUNIUPOKO AQUIFER WOULD BE AT 
89% OF THE SUSTAINABLE YIELD; AND WHEREAS, THE COUNCIL ADOPTED RESOLUTION 22-73 TO 
SUPPORT THE LAHAINA AQUIFER SECTOR AREA DESIGNATION AS SURFACE WATER AND 
GROUNDWATER MANAGEMENT AREA; AND WHEREAS, IN NOVEMBER 2022, THE STATE 
COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT FINED OLOWALU WATER COMPANY, INC. AS 
SUBSIDIARY OF WEST MAUI LAND COMPANY, INC.\r\n\r\n$470,050 FOR REPEATED VIOLATIONS 
INTERIM INSTREAM FLOW STANDARD FOR OLOWALU STREAM; AND WHEREAS, IN NOVEMBER 2022, 
THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE MANAGEMENT AMENDED IIFS FOR 12 STREAMS AND 
TRIBUTARIES IN HUELO REGION OF EAST MAUI AND EXPLORED HOW TO MODIFY THE EAST MAUI 
IRRIGATION SYSTEM TO BETTER PROTECT INSTREAM USES; AND WHEREAS, DEPUTY MANUEL WAS 
REDEPLOYED FROM HIS ROLE AS FIRST DEPUTY FOR THE COMMISSION ON WATER RESOURCE 
MANAGEMENT ON AUGUST 16, 2023 WITHOUT CAUSE; AND WHEREAS, IN A PRESS RELEASE ON

AND NATURAL RESOURCES STATED, "THAT HIS DEPLOYMENT DOES NOT SUGGEST THAT FIRST 
DEPUTY MANUEL DID ANYTHING WRONG." NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED BY THE COUNCIL
